### [178] [Magnetoresistance effect based on spin-selective transport in nanodevices using chiral molecules](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.23656)
*Mizuki Matsuzaka,Kotaro Kashima,Koki Terai,Takumi Ueda,Ryunosuke Miyamoto,Takashi Yamamoto,Kohei Sambe,Tomoyuki Akutagawa,Hideo Kaiju*

TL;DR: This study demonstrates the successful observation of the magnetoresistance effect in chiral molecules-based nanodevices using AFM, showing CISS-based MR devices with low magnetic fields. The results suggest potential applications in low-field MR devices and insights into the CISS mechanism.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The study aims to investigate the use of chirality-induced spin selectivity (CISS) in magnetoresistance (MR) devices, leveraging chiral molecules and advanced nanofabrication techniques to achieve low-field performance.

Method: ם филь.referenceö sharon the study involves the synthesis of a chiral molecule, fabrication of nanodevices with this molecule sandwiched between Ni78Fe22 and Au electrodes, and testing the MR effect using mc-AFM under low magnetic fields.

Result: The results show high spin selectivity in the thin films and successful observation of the MR effect in the nanodevices, correlating with the Ni78Fe22 electrode's magnetization states.

Conclusion: The findings suggest that CISS-based MR devices can operate at low magnetic fields, offering new perspectives on the mechanism of CISS and practical applications in MR devices.

Abstract: Recently, chirality-induced spin selectivity (CISS) has been observed in
chiral molecules and is attractive for application in magnetoresistance (MR)
devices. In this study, we fabricate CISS-based nanodevices consisting of
chiral molecules sandwiched between Ni78Fe22 and Au electrodes. Prior to device
fabrication, we have synthesized the chiral molecule
N-(3S)-3,7-dimethyloctyl[1]benzothieno[3,2-b]benzothiophene-2-carboxyamide
(S-BTBT-CONHR) and established a method for fabricating nanodevice electrodes.
We have successfully observed a high degree of spin selectivity in S-BTBT-CONHR
thin films using magnetic conductive atomic force microscopy (mc-AFM). By
combining chiral molecules with our advanced nanofabrication technique, we have
successfully fabricated Au/S-BTBT-CONHR/Ni78Fe22 nanodevices and observed the
MR effect in the fabricated devices under a low magnetic field at room
temperature. These MR curves correspond to the magnetization states of the
Ni78Fe22 electrode, indicating that the CISS-based MR effect is successfully
observed in the nanodevices under a low magnetic field. This study can lead to
the development of CISS-based MR devices under low magnetic fields and provide
new insights into the CISS effect mechanism on devices.

### [179] [Acoustic-Assisted Fabrication of Thin Shells with Spatially Distributed Imperfections](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.23828)
*Ilyes Krida,Jacob Tang,Daniel Floryan,Tian Chen*

Main category: physics.app-ph

TL;DR: 薄壳结构在生物系统中如甲虫甲壳和工程中广泛应用，具备 Operations research 和工程设计的能力。然而，由于微小几何缺陷，容易触发亚临界分叉失稳，影响承载能力。本文通过声波辅助制造方法，创造出具有空间分布、与振型相关的缺陷模式的薄壳结构，可以调节缺陷频率和幅度。实验表明，通过这种方法可以显著降低分叉压力，为工程设计提供有效方案。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 薄壳结构在多个领域中有重要应用，但几何缺陷敏感性研究不足，本文提出一种可调节缺陷模式的方法，用于提高结构耐受性。

Method: 利用声波辅助制造，将硅胶浇注到弹性模具上，振动导致流体流动产生厚度变化，使用高速成像和微CT扫描分析缺陷分布。

Result: 通过调整声波频率和体积可以调节缺陷几何和幅度，实验显示显著降低临界压力，提供研究和调整缺陷敏感性能力。

Conclusion: 本文提出了一种新的可控缺陷制造方法，用于调节薄壳结构的几何缺陷，改善其承载能力，为工程设计提供了有效参考。

Abstract: Thin-shell structures, found in biological systems such as beetle carapaces
and widely used in aerospace, civil, and mechanical engineering, achieve
remarkable strength-to-mass ratio given their slenderness and curved
geometries. However, their load-bearing capacity is highly sensitive to
geometric imperfections, which are often unavoidable during fabrication and can
trigger subcritical buckling. Silicone-based hemispherical domes have served as
an experimental modal system to study this phenomenon, yet prior work has
largely focused on localized dimples or flat imperfections, failing to capture
the spatially distributed nature of real-world imperfection patterns. Here, we
introduce an acoustic-assisted method for fabricating thin shells with
spatially distributed, vibrational mode-shaped imperfections. Silicone is cast
onto a thick elastic mold excited by a speaker, and vibration-induced flow
during curing creates thickness variations. High-speed imaging and microCT
scanning reveal accumulation of material at the antinodes of the mold's
vibrational modes. We show that imperfection geometry can be tuned by acoustic
frequency, while their amplitude increases with acoustic volume. Buckling
experiments demonstrate significant reductions in critical pressure, offering a
scalable platform to study and tune imperfection-sensitive mechanics. Beyond
shell mechanics, we offer a scalable and tunable fabrication method for
patterning soft materials in applications ranging from morphable surfaces to
bioinspired design.

</details>
